Library name /Nombre de la biblioteca: NCSU Libraries
Latitude / Latitud: 35.7875614999999

Website / Sitio web: http://www.lib.ncsu.edu/
Date / Fecha: November 1 2017
Time / Hora: 7pm - 9pm
Event info / Información del evento: Did you know that you can play the latest video games, right in your library? In celebration of International Games Week 2017, NCSU Libraries invites you to “Raiders of the Lost Arcade”, an informal, drop-in gaming session for gamers of all levels and interests. Held in the Fishbowl Forum of D. H. Hill Library, we will explore video games as a way to encourage experiential learning, empathy building, and consider narratives from an inclusive perspective. We will be playing a curated selection of Playstation and Steam games that explore different forms of “survival”, including The Last of Us, Dream Daddy, Portal 2, and This War of Mine. Critical discussion is encouraged, along with participation from those who are new to exploring video games. We also welcome those who just want to blow off some steam and have fun gaming! Pizza will be provided.

Prowadząca w Bibliotece Centralnej klub czytelniczy dla dzieci Mirosława Gąbka przygotowała na piątkowe popołudnie specjalne spotkanie klubu, podczas którego dzieci będą mogły poznać literackie gry planszowe. Zapraszamy serdecznie! Wstęp wolny.

Date / Fecha: 10/30/2017, 10/31/2017, 11/01/2017, 11/02/2017, 11/03/2017, 11/04/2017
Time / Hora: 6:30 pm - 8:00 pm, 3:00 pm - 4:30 pm, 3:00 pm - 4:30 pm, 6:30 pm - 8:00 pm, 3:00 pm - 4:30 pm, 10:00 am - 4:00 pm
Event info / Información del evento: Come Celebrate the American Library Association’s International Games Week at the Margaret E. Heggan Free Public Library October 30th through November 4th! We will be holding events all week long celebrating board, card, puzzle, computer and video games! Additionally, our Pokemon GO gym will be accepting challengers, our large collection of books about games and gaming will await you, and our Minecraft server will allow you to explore the realm of Hyrule! Monday October 30th 6:30PM-8:00PM: Let’s Play Dread Can you endure the horrors that creep into your own imagination? Join us as we kick off International Game Week with Dread, an innovative pen and paper role playing game that utilizes Jenga instead of dice. Tension rises as the narrative and tower alike aim to betray you! This program is open to Heggan Library card holders only. This program is open to all ages, patrons under the age of ten must be accompanied by an adult. Advanced Registration is Required. Tuesday, October 31, 2017: 3-4:30 PM: Escape the Library! What’s the newest ‘thing’ in gaming? ESCAPE ROOMS! Join us on October 31 for a creepy Halloween-themed escape room game. Participants will collaborate as a team to work out the puzzles. Can you solve the mystery and unlock the box? Costumes welcome and strongly encouraged. Prizes awarded to all who successfully escape. Program open to Heggan cardholders only, ages 11-18. Advance registration is required. Wednesday November 1st 3:00PM-4:30PM: Then and Now: The Oregon Trail A staple of any computer lab in the 80s and 90s, the Oregon Trail is one of the finest examples of “Edu-tainment” challenging players to survive a perilous journey by wagon from Independence Missouri to Willamette Valley in 1848. We will compare the original with the newly released card game to see which experience is superior. This program is open to Heggan Library card holders only. This program is open to all ages, patrons under the age of ten must be accompanied by an adult. Advanced Registration is Required. Thursday, November 2, 2017: 6:30 to 8 PM: Retro Game Night @ The Library Modern gaming has roots in board games and card games. Register for a totally tech-free night of gaming, and play some of your favorite board and card games. Snacks will be available. Program open to Heggan cardholders only, ages 11-18. Advance registration is required. Friday November 3rd 3:00PM-4:30PM: The Heggan Library Plays Pokemon Come in for an afternoon fit for Pokemon Masters! We will work together to play Pokemon Sapphire by making decisions democratically, button press by button press. What direction will this organized chaos take our adventure? Come in to find out! This program is open to Heggan Library card holders only. This program is open to all ages, patrons under the age of ten must be accompanied by an adult. Advanced Registration is Required. Saturday November 4th International Game Week Finale Free for All! Celebrate the conclusion of International Game Week with a day of gaming events at the library! 10AM-11:30PM—Board Game Round Up: Start the day with some of our favorite board games! 11:30AM-1:30PM-- Super Smash Brothers Free for All: Enjoy a battle royale of your favorite Nintendo characters and more! 1:30PM-2:30PM-- Gamer Trivia: Put your knowledge of games and gaming to the test! 2:30PM-4PM—Five Nights At Freddy’s 20/20/20/20/20/20/20/20/20/20 Mode Challenge: Can you withstand the collective might of all of the horrors of Freddy Fazbear’s Pizza at their most fearsome? These programs are open to Heggan Library card holders only. These programs are open to all ages, patrons under the age of ten must be accompanied by an adult. Advanced Registration is Required.

Library name /Nombre de la biblioteca: Window on America center in DOUNB Library
Latitude / Latitud: 48.464717
Longitude / Longitud: 35.0461829999999
Website / Sitio web: http://www.libr.dp.ua/main.htm
Date / Fecha: Nov. 11th, 11/11
Time / Hora: 2:00 pm - 4:00 pm
Event info / Información del evento: on November, 11 – ESC Gabfest: INTERNATIONAL GAMES DAY at WOA Dnipro. This afternoon the Gabfest Club members in Dnipro Window on America center observed the Games Day @your library. The group was introduced to the iconic American board games “Monopoly” and “Scrabble”. The group was particularly impressed with the scandalous history behind the “Monopoly” game. The “Beatles” played “Monopoly” in their hotel room on their first U.S. tour. The game was even used to smuggle maps and money to POWs in World War II. And it turns out the game's modern version is nothing like it was supposed to be. The second game introduced to the group was “Scrabble”. It was created in 1938 by American architect Alfred Mosher Butts as a variation on an earlier word game called Lexiko. According to legend, Scrabble's big break came in 1952 when Jack Straus, president of Macy's department store, played the game on vacation. Upon returning from vacation, he was surprised to find that his store did not carry the game. He placed a large order and within a year, "everyone had to have one". The Club members watched the illustrative videos about the games and shared their own experiences of playing Monopoly or Scrabble. In the second part of the session the Club members were offered to play Activate games for English learners. The new WOA’s transforming furniture allowed to form smaller tables for several teams of players. The highlight of the session was the presentation of the display with the WOA’s games. The centerpieces of the display are Monopoly and Scrabble. The session was educational both for fluent speakers and the beginners. Participants number – 25 persons.
